## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: This task belongs to population ecology, where it studies the population growth rate over time. The physical relationship between variables is that the growth rate is dependent on the current population size and possibly time.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP/dt = c0 * P (population growth without density dependence)
- Logistic growth: dP/dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) (population growth with carrying capacity)
- Ricker model: dP/dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 - c2 * P) (population growth with non-linear density dependence)
- Gompertz equation: dP/dt = c0 * P * ln(c1 / P) (population growth with sigmoidal growth curve)
- Verhulst equation: dP/dt = c0 * P * (1 - (P / c1)**2) (population growth with symmetric sigmoidal growth curve)
- Sigmoidal growth: dP/dt = c0 * P**c1 / (P**c1 + c2) (population growth with smooth transition to saturation)
- Malthusian law: dP/dt = c0 * P (population growth without density dependence, constant growth rate)
- Simplified SIR model: dP/dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) * (c2 - P / c3) (population growth with disease dynamics)
- von Bertalanffy growth equation: dP/dt = c0 * (c1 - P**c2) (population growth with non-linear growth curve)
- Monod equation: dP/dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (population growth with Michaelis-Menten kinetics)
- Holling type II functional response: dP/dt = c0 * P * c1 * P / (c2 + P**2) (population growth with predator-prey dynamics)
- Holling type III functional response: dP/dt = c0 * P * c1 * P**2 / (c2 + P**3) (population growth with predator-prey dynamics)
- Sigmoidal logistic growth: dP/dt = c0 * P * (1 - (P / c1)**c2) (population growth with smooth transition to saturation)

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.9198(1 - P/84.03)P + \frac{0.9198 P^2}{7.531P + 1}$$

Let me expand this:
$$f(P) = 0.9198P - \frac{0.9198}{84.03}P^2 + \frac{0.9198 P^2}{7.531P + 1}$$
$$= 0.9198P - 0.01095P^2 + \frac{0.9198 P^2}{7.531P + 1}$$

Let me combine over a common denominator $(7.531P + 1)$:
$$= \frac{(0.9198P - 0.01095P^2)(7.531P + 1) + 0.9198P^2}{7.531P + 1}$$

Numerator:
$$= 0.9198P \cdot 7.531P + 0.9198P - 0.01095P^2 \cdot 7.531P - 0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P^2$$
$$= 6.927P^2 + 0.9198P - 0.08246P^3 - 0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P^2$$
$$= -0.08246P^3 + (6.927 + 0.9198 - 0.01095)P^2 + 0.9198P$$
$$= -0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P$$

So: $f(P) = \frac{P(-0.08246P^2 + 7.836P + 0.9198)}{7.531P + 1}$

The GT is a **rational function** of P (degree 3 numerator / degree 1 denominator), which can also be written as a quadratic polynomial plus a term $\frac{aP^2}{bP+c}$.

Key structural features:
- It's a function of P only (not t)
- It's a rational function equivalent to: quadratic in P + rational term $\frac{P^2}{linear(P)}$

Let me now check which candidates can match this structure.

### Candidates with rational function structure (8-15)

**Candidate 8:** $\frac{Pc_0 + c_1 + (Pc_2+1)(P^2c_3 + Pc_4 + P + c_5)}{Pc_2+1}$

Simplify: $= P^2c_3 + Pc_4 + P + c_5 + \frac{Pc_0 + c_1}{Pc_2 + 1}$

$= c_3P^2 + (c_4+1)P + c_5 + \frac{c_0P + c_1}{c_2P + 1}$

GT = $aP^2 + bP + \frac{dP^2}{eP + 1}$ where $a = -0.01095$, $b = 0.9198$, $d = 0.9198$, $e = 7.531$.

For the rational part: GT has $\frac{dP^2}{eP+1}$, candidate has $\frac{c_0P + c_1}{c_2P + 1}$. The numerator degree differs (2 vs 1). Cannot match.

Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 9:** $\frac{c_0 + (Pc_1+1)(P^2c_2 + Pc_3 + P + c_4)}{Pc_1+1}$

Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 10:** $\frac{c_0 + (Pc_1+c_2)(P(Pc_3+c_4)+c_5)}{Pc_1+c_2}$

$= c_3P^2 + c_4P + c_5 + \frac{c_0}{c_1P+c_2}$

Rational part: $\frac{c_0}{c_1P+c_2}$. GT needs $\frac{P^2}{...}$. No match.

**Candidate 11:** $\frac{c_0 + (Pc_1+c_2)(P^2c_3+Pc_4+c_5)}{Pc_1+c_2}$

**Candidate 12:** $\frac{P(P^2c_0 + (Pc_1+c_2)(Pc_3+c_4))}{Pc_3+c_4}$

$= \frac{P \cdot P^2c_0}{Pc_3+c_4} + P(Pc_1+c_2)$

$= \frac{c_0P^3}{c_3P+c_4} + c_1P^2 + c_2P$

GT = $\frac{-0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P}{7.531P+1}$

Can we write this as $\frac{c_0P^3}{c_3P+c_4} + c_1P^2 + c_2P$?

$= \frac{c_0P^3 + (c_1P^2+c_2P)(c_3P+c_4)}{c_3P+c_4}$

$= \frac{c_0P^3 + c_1c_3P^3 + c_1c_4P^2 + c_2c_3P^2 + c_2c_4P}{c_3P+c_4}$

$= \frac{(c_0+c_1c_3)P^3 + (c_1c_4+c_2c_3)P^2 + c_2c_4P}{c_3P+c_4}$

Compare with GT: $\frac{-0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P}{7.531P+1}$

So: $c_3 = 7.531$, $c_4 = 1$, $c_2 \cdot 1 = 0.9198 \Rightarrow c_2 = 0.9198$, $c_1 \cdot 1 + 0.9198 \cdot 7.531 = 7.836 \Rightarrow c_1 = 7.836 - 6.927 = 0.909$, $c_0 + 0.909 \cdot 7.531 = -0.08246 \Rightarrow c_0 = -0.08246 - 6.845 = -6.928$.

Let me verify: $(c_0+c_1c_3) = -6.928 + 0.909 \times 7.531 = -6.928 + 6.845 = -0.083$ ✓
$(c_1c_4+c_2c_3) = 0.909 + 0.9198 \times 7.531 = 0.909 + 6.927 = 7.836$ ✓
$c_2c_4 = 0.9198$ ✓

**Candidate 12 matches!**

Candidate 12 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 13:** $\frac{P(c_0 + (Pc_1+c_2)(Pc_3+1))}{Pc_3+1}$

$= c_1P^2 + c_2P + \frac{c_0P}{c_3P+1}$

GT needs $\frac{P^2}{...}$ in the rational part, but this has $\frac{P}{...}$. Can't match degree.

Wait, let me reconsider. GT = $c_aP^2 + c_bP + \frac{c_dP^2}{c_eP+1}$. Candidate has $c_1P^2 + c_2P + \frac{c_0P}{c_3P+1}$. The rational parts differ in numerator degree.

Candidate 13 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 14:** $\frac{P(Pc_0(P+c_1) + Pc_2 + c_3(P+c_1))}{P+c_1}$

Expand numerator inside: $P(c_0P^2 + c_0c_1P + c_2P + c_3P + c_3c_1)$
$= P(c_0P^2 + (c_0c_1+c_2+c_3)P + c_3c_1)$

So: $\frac{c_0P^3 + (c_0c_1+c_2+c_3)P^2 + c_3c_1P}{P+c_1}$

Compare with GT: $\frac{-0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P}{7.531P+1}$

Denominator: $P + c_1$. GT denominator: $7.531P + 1$. We can write $7.531P + 1 = 7.531(P + 1/7.531)$. So $c_1 = 1/7.531 = 0.1328$.

But then we need to scale the numerator by $1/7.531$:
$\frac{-0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P}{7.531(P+0.1328)}$

So numerator coefficients divided by 7.531:
$c_0 = -0.08246/7.531 = -0.01095$
$c_3c_1 = 0.9198/7.531 = 0.1221 \Rightarrow c_3 = 0.1221/0.1328 = 0.9194$
$c_0c_1 + c_2 + c_3 = 7.836/7.531 = 1.0405$
$-0.01095 \times 0.1328 + c_2 + 0.9194 = 1.0405$
$c_2 = 1.0405 - 0.9194 + 0.001454 = 0.1225$

Let me verify the full numerator:
$c_0P^3 = -0.01095P^3$
$(c_0c_1+c_2+c_3)P^2 = (-0.001454 + 0.1225 + 0.9194)P^2 = 1.0405P^2$
$c_3c_1P = 0.9194 \times 0.1328 P = 0.1221P$

Full fraction: $\frac{-0.01095P^3 + 1.0405P^2 + 0.1221P}{P + 0.1328}$

Multiply by $7.531$: should give $\frac{-0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9198P}{7.531P + 1}$... wait, that's not right. Let me redo.

$\frac{-0.01095P^3 + 1.0405P^2 + 0.1221P}{P + 0.1328} = \frac{7.531 \times (-0.01095P^3 + 1.0405P^2 + 0.1221P)}{7.531(P + 0.1328)} = \frac{-0.08246P^3 + 7.836P^2 + 0.9195P}{7.531P + 1}$

This matches GT! ✓

Candidate 14 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 15:** $\frac{P(c_0 + (Pc_1+c_2)(Pc_3+c_4))}{Pc_3+c_4}$

$= P\left(\frac{c_0}{Pc_3+c_4} + Pc_1 + c_2\right) = c_1P^2 + c_2P + \frac{c_0P}{c_3P+c_4}$

Rational part has $P$ numerator, GT needs $P^2$. No match.

Candidate 15 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Now let me check the exponential/transcendental candidates. The GT is purely rational, so any candidate with exp, sin, cos, log, tanh, sqrt that can't be zeroed out won't match.

**Candidate 1:** $P(Pc_0+c_1) + c_2\sin(Pc_3+c_4) + c_5\log(\frac{P+c_6(Pc_7+c_8)}{P})$

$= c_0P^2 + c_1P + c_2\sin(Pc_3+c_4) + c_5\log(1 + c_6c_7 + \frac{c_6c_8}{P})$

Set $c_2 = 0$ to kill sin. Then: $c_0P^2 + c_1P + c_5\log(1 + c_6c_7 + c_6c_8/P)$.

The log term can't produce a rational function. Set $c_5 = 0$ too: just $c_0P^2 + c_1P$, which is a polynomial, not matching GT.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** $c_0P^2 + c_1P + c_2\log(c_3\exp(c_4/P)+1) + c_5\exp(c_6/P)$

The log and exp terms involve transcendental functions of $1/P$. These can't produce a rational function. Setting them to zero gives just a polynomial.

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** Similar transcendental terms. No match.

Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** $c_0P^2 + c_1P + c_2\exp(c_3/P^2) + c_4\exp(c_5/P)$

Exponentials can't produce rational functions. Setting to zero gives polynomial only.

Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 5:** Same structure as 4.

Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 6:** Has exp and cos. No match.

Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 7:** $c_0P^2 + c_1P + c_2\log(\frac{P+c_3}{P}) + c_4\exp(c_5/P)$

$= c_0P^2 + c_1P + c_2\log(1+c_3/P) + c_4\exp(c_5/P)$

Transcendental. No match.

Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 16:** $\frac{c_0\exp(Pc_1) + (Pc_2+c_3)(P^2c_4+Pc_5+c_6)}{Pc_2+c_3}$

$= P^2c_4 + Pc_5 + c_6 + \frac{c_0\exp(Pc_1)}{Pc_2+c_3}$

Set $c_0 = 0$: polynomial. Not enough. Can't match GT.

Candidate 16 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 17:** $\frac{Pc_0+c_1+(Pc_2+c_3)(P^2c_4+Pc_5+c_6\exp(c_7/P))}{Pc_2+c_3}$

$= P^2c_4 + Pc_5 + c_6\exp(c_7/P) + \frac{Pc_0+c_1}{Pc_2+c_3}$

Has exp term. Set $c_6 = 0$: $P^2c_4 + Pc_5 + \frac{c_0P+c_1}{c_2P+c_3}$. Rational part has linear numerator, GT needs quadratic. No match.

Candidate 17 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 18-50:** Let me quickly scan for rational-only candidates.

**Candidate 19:** Has $t$ dependence. Set $c_0 = 0, c_6 = 0$: $\frac{c_1 + (P(Pc_2+c_3)+c_4\exp(c_5/P)) \cdot c_7}{c_7}$. Still has exp. Set $c_4 = 0$: $\frac{c_1}{c_7} + Pc_2P + c_3P = c_2P^2 + c_3P + c_1/c_7$. Polynomial only. No match.

Candidate 19 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidates 18, 20-50:** All contain transcendental functions (exp, sin, cos, log, tanh, sqrt). The GT is purely rational. The only way to match is if the transcendental parts can be zeroed out, leaving a polynomial, which can't match the rational GT.

Let me double-check candidates 28, 29, 30, 32-36, 39, 41, 44, 47.

**Candidate 28:** $c_0P^2 + c_1 + c_2\exp(c_3/P) + c_4(P+c_5)^2$

Set $c_2 = 0$: $(c_0+c_4)P^2 + 2c_4c_5P + c_1 + c_4c_5^2$. Polynomial. No match.

**Candidate 29:** $c_0P^2 + P + c_1\exp(c_2/P) + c_3(P+c_4)$

Set $c_1 = 0$: $c_0P^2 + (1+c_3)P + c_3c_4$. Polynomial. No match.

**Candidate 34/35:** $c_0P^2 + c_1P + c_2\exp(c_3/P) + c_4$. Set $c_2 = 0$: polynomial. No match.

**Candidate 39:** $c_0P^2 + c_1P + c_2 + c_3\log(\frac{P+c_4}{P})$

$= c_0P^2 + c_1P + c_2 + c_3\log(1+c_4/P)$. Log is transcendental. Set $c_3 = 0$: polynomial. No match.

**Candidate 41:** $c_0P^2 + P^2 + c_1P + \frac{c_2}{|P+c_3|} + c_4$

With $P \geq 0$ and choosing $c_3 > 0$: $(c_0+1)P^2 + c_1P + c_4 + \frac{c_2}{P+c_3}$

GT = $aP^2 + bP + \frac{dP^2}{eP+1}$. The rational part here is $\frac{c_2}{P+c_3}$ (constant numerator) vs $\frac{P^2}{...}$ in GT. No match.

Candidate 41 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 44:** $c_0P^2 + c_1P\exp(c_2/P) + c_3 + c_4/P$

Transcendental. No match.

**Candidate 47:** $P(Pc_0 + P + c_1) + c_2\exp(c_3/P) + c_4$

Set $c_2 = 0$: $(c_0+1)P^2 + c_1P + c_4$. Polynomial. No match.

**Candidate 48:** Has $t$ and log/exp. Complex. Even zeroing $t$ terms, has log(exp) which is transcendental.

**Candidate 51:** $\frac{c_0 + (Pc_1+c_2)(P(Pc_3+c_4)+c_5\sin(Pc_6+c_7))}{Pc_1+c_2}$

Set $c_5 = 0$: $P(Pc_3+c_4) + \frac{c_0}{Pc_1+c_2} = c_3P^2 + c_4P + \frac{c_0}{c_1P+c_2}$

Rational part: constant numerator. No match.

Candidate 51 verdict: [NO MATCH]
